  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_649f5354-c576-4055-9e4a-5f87ddc5eb2a'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14930837653664502433"><b>In the tradition of The Girl on the Train, The Silent Wife, and Gone Girl comes an enthralling psychological thriller that spins one woman's seemingly good fortune and another woman's mysterious fate through a kaleidoscope of duplicity, death, and deception.<br/><br/>Soon to be a major motion picture directed by Ron Howard.</b><br/><br/><i>Please make a list of every possession you consider essentia</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14930837653664502433" style="display:none"><b>In the tradition of The Girl on the Train, The Silent Wife, and Gone Girl comes an enthralling psychological thriller that spins one woman's seemingly good fortune and another woman's mysterious fate through a kaleidoscope of duplicity, death, and deception.<br /><br />Soon to be a major motion picture directed by Ron Howard.</b><br /><br /><i>Please make a list of every possession you consider essential to your life.</i><br /><br />The request seems odd, even intrusive - and for the two women who answer, the consequences are devastating.<br /><br /><b>Emma</b><br /><br />Reeling from a traumatic break-in, Emma wants a new place to live. But none of the apartments she sees are affordable or feel safe. Until One Folgate Street. The house is an architectural masterpiece: a minimalist design of pale stone, plate glass, and soaring ceilings. But there are rules. The enigmatic architect who designed the house retains full control: no books, no throw pillows, no photos or clutter or personal effects of any kind. The space is intended to transform its occupant - and it does.<br /><br /><b>Jane</b><br /><br />After a personal tragedy, Jane needs a fresh start. When she finds One Folgate Street, she is instantly drawn to the space - and to its aloof but seductive creator. Moving in, Jane soon learns about the untimely death of the home's previous tenant, a woman similar to Jane in age and appearance. As Jane tries to untangle truth from lies, she unwittingly follows the same patterns, makes the same choices, crosses paths with the same people, and experiences the same terror as the girl before.<br /><br /><i>Listening Length: 9 hours and 59 minutes</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14930837653664502433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/914673-why-oh-why-do-the-authors-keep-writing">Why oh Why do the authors keep writing titles with the word &quot;Girl&quot; in it??? I won&#39;t even look at these books because it&#39;s just gotten to be so ridiculous. After all that work of writing the novel why settle for a stereotypical name, I just don&#39;t get it!</a>

The<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The "girl" in this title has a double meaning though, which you learn at the end. I don't think it's as "denigrating" to women as one might think. There's a twist.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_361').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_1837364110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1837364110" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1837364110?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1837364110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13316576960402864869"><blockquote>
  <i>"Yes, daddy. Yes."</i>
</blockquote><br/>No. Please no. <br/><br/>I feel like somebody noted the success of books like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gone Girl</a> and the success of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10818853.Fifty_Shades_of_Grey__Fifty_Shades___1_' title='Fifty Shades of Grey (Fifty Shades, #1) by E.L. James' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fifty Shades of Grey</a> and thought: wouldn't it be great if we had a book that combined the two? No, actually. No, it wouldn't.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28016509.The_Girl_Before' title='The Girl Before by J.P. Delaney' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl Before</a> failed on so many levels, and I say that as a reluctant fan of these "domestic thrillers". I've enjoyed everything from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train' title='The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl on the Train</a> to last year's ridiculous but fast-paced <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29437949.Behind_Closed_Doors' title='Behind Closed Doors by B.A. Paris' rel='nofollow noopener'>Behind Closed Doors</a>. I expected I'd like this one too, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText13316576960402864869" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Yes, daddy. Yes."</i>
</blockquote><br />No. Please no. <br /><br />I feel like somebody noted the success of books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a> and the success of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10818853.Fifty_Shades_of_Grey__Fifty_Shades___1_" title="Fifty Shades of Grey (Fifty Shades, #1) by E.L. James" rel="nofollow noopener">Fifty Shades of Grey</a> and thought: wouldn't it be great if we had a book that combined the two? No, actually. No, it wouldn't.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28016509.The_Girl_Before" title="The Girl Before by J.P. Delaney" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl Before</a> failed on so many levels, and I say that as a reluctant fan of these "domestic thrillers". I've enjoyed everything from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl on the Train</a> to last year's ridiculous but fast-paced <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29437949.Behind_Closed_Doors" title="Behind Closed Doors by B.A. Paris" rel="nofollow noopener">Behind Closed Doors</a>. I expected I'd like this one too, but all I got was a <b>weird relationship with "rules"</b>, another guy called <b>Edward</b>, and <b>transparent twists</b>.<br /><br />The book alternates between the perspectives of Emma (Before) and Jane (After) as they move into the techno-minimalist apartment at One Folgate Street. Though beautiful, there is almost no furniture, absolutely everything is digital, and most bizarre of all - the landlord and famous architect, Edward Monkford, requires that his tenants follow some very strict rules. Both women soon find themselves caught up in a love affair with Edward, but when Jane discovers that Emma died in the apartment, she can't help investigating further.<br /><br />Jane's digging uncovers some disturbing facts about Emma - she expressed concern over Edward's controlling ways to her psychiatrist, her death may not have been an accident, and strangest of all, she looked eerily like Jane herself.<br /><br />Firstly, I don't know what is wrong with these women. Without giving away twists, their behaviour is often outright ridiculous. Warning bells are going off left, right and centre, and they're completely oblivious. At worst, Edward is a murderer, but even at best, he's a creepy weirdo. It's almost comical how much he resembles Christian Grey - not just sexually dominant and prone to "losing control" but also strict about Emma and Jane's eating and exercise habits. Ick. Get out. Also, lots of people have a "type", but it's just plain weird if your "type" are all women who look virtually identical. <br /><br />Secondly, <b>there is no atmosphere</b>. I feel like the author tried to create a "creepy house with a dark history" feeling, but it didn't come through because so much of the book was nothing more than a weird romance. I also see how Delaney was trying to create a "ghost of past lovers" vibe, but this ain't no <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2001717.Daphne_du_Maurier" title="Daphne du Maurier" rel="nofollow noopener">Daphne du Maurier</a>. The writing wasn't strong enough to make you scared for the characters, to keep you metaphorically looking over your shoulder.<br /><br />It is often really difficult to distinguish between the two perspectives. I had to keep flicking to the beginning of the chapter to find out whether I was on Emma or Jane. This is partly because the <b>style is impersonal</b> and doesn't deeply connect you with the characters, but also partly because their stories are very similar. As we soon see, Edward takes them to the same places, gives them the same food, treats them the same ways - it was like reading the same perspective twice.<br /><br />And there's a whole bunch of subtle racism going on, as well as a bunch of other distasteful issues. If you insist on only writing about white, middle class people, don’t make the criminals/rapists black and working class. How do you not see what's wrong with that? And casual comments like this (made by a psychiatrist): <i>"In any relationship there are two repetition compulsions at work - his and hers."</i> I can think of a whole lot of relationships where that definitely isn't true.<br /><br />Plus, there's a really poor and insensitive <b>use of rape as a plot device</b>. Without giving away spoilers, someone who was seen to be orally raped is then making jokes about preferring human sperm sacs (to fish sperm sacs - it's a long story, Japanese restaurant, blah blah). Firstly... gross. And secondly... gross.<br /><br />But maybe, even after all of this, I could have been persuaded to up my rating if the ending had provided us with an interesting and satisfying reveal. Unfortunately, <b>I saw it coming from a mile away</b>. The list of suspects is too short; the list of suspects who we'd actually care about it being is even shorter. I'm sorry, but I can't even find anything good to say about it.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13316576960402864869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1836064687" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1836064687" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1836064687?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32054243-the-girl-before">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=horrible-ending">horrible-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=suspense-mystery-thriller">suspense-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836064687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7709986979314127432">I’m tossing this one on the heaping pile of books that led me to believe they were worthy of comparisons to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gone Girl</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train' title='The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl on the Train</a>, but left me disappointed instead. Is this madness ever going to end? Why can’t a book be left to stand on it’s own merits? I guess it’s my fault for giving in and picking up yet another ‘Girl’ book. Have no fear though, <b>once again, I’ve landed in the minority</b>, as the reviews I’ve seen have been overwhelming positive and apparently it’s being made into a </span>
  <span id="freeText7709986979314127432" style="display:none">I’m tossing this one on the heaping pile of books that led me to believe they were worthy of comparisons to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl on the Train</a>, but left me disappointed instead. Is this madness ever going to end? Why can’t a book be left to stand on it’s own merits? I guess it’s my fault for giving in and picking up yet another ‘Girl’ book. Have no fear though, <b>once again, I’ve landed in the minority</b>, as the reviews I’ve seen have been overwhelming positive and apparently it’s being made into a movie. So, <b>take this review with a grain of salt</b>. It’s just one reader’s thoughts and feelings, after all.<br /><br />Point blank - I don’t get it. <b>This whole scenario is strange. Odd. Completely ridiculous.</b> What sane person would agree to live in this situation? Forget sane - why would anybody sign up for this?<br /><br />Maybe I’m the crazy one, but there is no way I would ever agree to give up most of my belongings to move in to a minimalistic stone box of a house that comes with over 200 stipulations. Restrictive and ridiculous rules. Not to mention, answering a bizarre questionnaire and having my “amenities” shut down every time the perfectionistic control freak of a landlord feels like I need to answer yet another series of questions. All in an effort to gauge my “growth” or acceptance of the lifestyle the house demands. I don’t care how good looking or how famous of an architect the owner is; I wouldn’t do it. The author sells the idea by garnering sympathy from the reader for the two women and the excitement of top of the line technology - it's the ultimate smart house. Both women have recently experienced tragedies and need a fresh start. And, of course, the rent for this pseudo stone cell is quite cheap. Hmm . . . I wonder why?<br /><br />The story unfolds through the eyes of the two women - Emma, the previous tenant, and Jane, the current tenant. The story flip-flops between then and now, which takes place two years apart, at a pretty rapid pace. We get to see how their stories mirror each other and it’s a little convoluted at times. More than once, I had to go back to the beginning of the chapter to see whose head I was in because I was kind of lost. I liked the whole notion of getting caught up in a story or your past and recreating or reliving that same story over and over. But that’s were the likes kind of ended for me.<br /><br />The entire plot felt like a tangled mess and not one I particularly enjoyed unraveling. Albeit, there was something about it that kept me turning the pages. I can’t say I was wowed though - not by the characters, the scenario or even the twist. <b>I failed to see what so many others have found exceptional about this one.</b><br /><br /><i>*THANK YOU to Random House/Ballantine Books and NetGalley for an ARC in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7709986979314127432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1920804064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1920804064" />
    <a title="Deanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15662887-deanna"><img alt="Deanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437589889p2/15662887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1920804064?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1920804064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9966365145092461949">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/'>https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br/><br/>4.5 Stars!! <br/><br/>The Girl Before is a psychological thriller that is getting a lot of attention. The movie rights have even been sold to Universal with Ron Howard to direct. I didn't know any of that when I first read the description for the book. I just thought it sounded like an entertaining read.<br/><br/><em>"Please make a list of every possession you consider essential to your life."</em><br/><br/>One Folgate Street in London, is a high-tech minimalist </span>
  <span id="freeText9966365145092461949" style="display:none">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/">https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br /><br />4.5 Stars!! <br /><br />The Girl Before is a psychological thriller that is getting a lot of attention. The movie rights have even been sold to Universal with Ron Howard to direct. I didn't know any of that when I first read the description for the book. I just thought it sounded like an entertaining read.<br /><br /><em>"Please make a list of every possession you consider essential to your life."</em><br /><br />One Folgate Street in London, is a high-tech minimalist house with so many cool amenities and features that you would figure the rent would be sky-high. But the rent is actually very reasonable.<br /><br />So what's the catch? Well there's no catch really...<br /><br />Except for THE RULES!!<br /><br />Tenants are required to follow very a list of very strict rules. Things like no pets, paying rent on time, no loud noise after 11pm, take out the garbage. You know, things like that...<br /><br />NOPE...not at all like that.<br /><br />There are over 200 rules that tenants MUST be abide by in order to live in the house.<br /><br />To say that the owner/landlord of One Folgate Street is picky about who lives in the house is an understatement. To say that he's a bit particular about his rules for the tenants is putting it mildly. The rental application is extremely long and includes many bizarre (and impossible) questions.<br /><br /><em>"A person close to you confesses in confidence that they ran someone over while drunk. As a result they have given up drinking for good. Would you feel obliged to report it to the police?"</em><br /><br />Is it worth it to live in such a beautiful high-tech home? This home with its awesome hidden gadgets. A house cleaner comes weekly. The lights, heat and cooling will set to tenants personal preferences. The shower will also adjust to their personal settings. Even the air in the house makes you feel better with its ultrasonic - mood enhancing waveforms.<br /><br /><em>"Imagine a hospital where the structure itself becomes part of the healing process, or a home for dementia sufferers that actually helps them to remember. This house might be simple, but it's ambition is extraordinary."</em><br /><br />Just don't forget.....the RULES. The main one? NO CLUTTER! Everything has its place, usually out of sight. So no pictures, no plants, no ornaments, no books....wait NO BOOKS???? (OMG!!! that's just wrong!)<br /><br />The owner, Edward Monkford is the architect who built the house. He also lives a minimalist lifestyle. He will not rent unless he finds the perfect tenant. But his need for control goes so much farther than that. And yet... some people are drawn to the "tormented genius". But who is Edward really? What happens if someone does break the rules?<br /><br />Emma and her boyfriend, Simon are looking for a safe place to live after a recent break-in. However, their budget is a bit tight and everything is either horrible or too expensive. Then the agent shows them One Folgate Street. She explains the lengthy process for application. Simon is hesitant but Emma feels like the place might be exactly what they need. The rules make her feel secure. She wants to reinvent herself, bring order to her life, to change and be a better person.<br /><br />The house may change her, but will it be for the better?<br /><br />We then meet Jane. After a devastating loss, Jane is looking for new place to live. She wants to make a new start and hopes that One Folgate Street is the place to do it. But it's not long before some strange things start happening. Jane learns some of the dark history of the house and is determined to find out more, especially what happened to the previous tenant.<br /><br />The house may be inexpensive and full of high-tech gadgets, but the walls of the house are also full of secrets. Where is the previous tenant? and is Jane in any danger?<br /><br /><em>"That's all anyone's looking for really, isn't it? Someone to take care of the mess inside our heads?"</em><br /><br />This book may not be for everyone. There is a lot of sex. I will definitely say that some of the characters "turn-ons" may be "turn-offs" for some readers. It wasn't really my thing and I could have done without those parts. However, it didn't really interfere with my enjoyment of the rest of the book.<br /><br />The chapters alternate between THEN and NOW and are narrated by Jane (NOW) and Emma (THEN). I flew through the pages. Occasionally I had to flip back to double-check whether it was Emma or Jane but most of the time I was able to keep up. The story may have been hard to believe and far-fetched at times, but I decided to try to go with the flow and enjoy it...<br /><br />In the end I really liked this novel. I was pulled and it got right inside my head. I had to know what was going to happen! A thrilling story about a house I would NEVER want to live in, (seriously I could not handle any of the rules) but I sure enjoyed reading about it.<br /><br />P.S Put your shampoo away<br /><br />Thank you, Ballantine Books for providing an advanced copy of this book for me to read in exchange for my honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9966365145092461949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1811598617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1811598617" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1811598617?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1811598617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6394598439587774573">1 Folgate Street is no ordinary house, it is cutting edge and won the Stirling Prize. It is an example of extreme minimalism and incorporates the latest home technology. It was originally designed by the techno-architect Edward Monkton as his family home but his wife and son died there which means its now available for others to live. Only there is the slight problem of over 200 conditions that have to be adhered to by whoever lives there. And they have to be interviewed and approved by Monkton </span>
  <span id="freeText6394598439587774573" style="display:none">1 Folgate Street is no ordinary house, it is cutting edge and won the Stirling Prize. It is an example of extreme minimalism and incorporates the latest home technology. It was originally designed by the techno-architect Edward Monkton as his family home but his wife and son died there which means its now available for others to live. Only there is the slight problem of over 200 conditions that have to be adhered to by whoever lives there. And they have to be interviewed and approved by Monkton personally. <br /><br />The narrative focuses on Emma from the past, and Jane in the present. Both are troubled women. Emma was held at knife point by burglars and she is struggling to come to terms with this. This event drives her decision to apply to live in the house, despite her boyfriend, Simon's reservations. The conditions for residing there will turn her into a new person with more control, Jane has had a stillborn baby and grieving. This house will be her new start and she just happens to fancy the architect. She is receiving a flower delivery of gentians which she assumes is from the architect until she reads the card....and realises there is more to the house than she thought. Emma died in the house.<br /><br />A concerned Jane begins to investigate Emma, the girl before to ascertain whether she was murdered, and if so by whom. There are uncomfortable similarities between her and Emma. From both resembling Edward's wife, to having a no strings attached affair with him which runs a similar if not identical course, to both having risque sex. Jane meets the people in Emma's life including Simon, the aggrieved boyfriend, and Carol, the therapist. Meanwhile, the house appears to develop an entity of its own as strange and random things happen. Is the controlling and manipulative Edward a killer? Is Emma a reliable narrator? An air of menace hangs over the house as danger begins to close in around Jane. <br /><br />The writing is lucid, sparse and beautiful. Pretty much like the house, and there is an air of claustrophobia in the story. This is a house with tragic beginnings and a strong character that is destined to trouble those who live there, you can just feel this. It is a good psychological thriller that keeps you reading without ever losing interest. Thanks to Quercus for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6394598439587774573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2221891398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2221891398" />
    <a title="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara"><img alt="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537347712p2/43416866.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2221891398?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" href="/user/show/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara">Evgnossia O&#39;Hara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2221891398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17576168458665224347">Review was originally published on <a href='https://throughthechapters.wordpress.com/2017/12/31/the-girl-before-by-j-p-delaneyreview/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Through the Chapters|Blog</a><br/><br/>This book was on my TBR for almost a year. I expected it to be a very good psychological thriller since it was compared to the “Gone Girl” one of the most mind-blowing books I have ever read. Unfortunately, I wasn’t only disappointed. I was frustrated, and let me explain why.<br/><br/>This story follows two women Emma and Jane, who wanted to escape the tragic events of their past, in order to begin a new life in a new apartment. The narration rot</span>
  <span id="freeText17576168458665224347" style="display:none">Review was originally published on <a href="https://throughthechapters.wordpress.com/2017/12/31/the-girl-before-by-j-p-delaneyreview/" rel="nofollow noopener">Through the Chapters|Blog</a><br><br>This book was on my TBR for almost a year. I expected it to be a very good psychological thriller since it was compared to the “Gone Girl” one of the most mind-blowing books I have ever read. Unfortunately, I wasn’t only disappointed. I was frustrated, and let me explain why.<br><br>This story follows two women Emma and Jane, who wanted to escape the tragic events of their past, in order to begin a new life in a new apartment. The narration rotates between those two ladies, to show us the events of past (Emma) and present (Jane). They were presented to the audience so desperate, that they agree to move to an apartment, at One Folgate Street with weird and ridiculous rules, as tenants. They were so deep into their grief and post traumatic syndrome that they were completely ok by signing a contract with 200 rules such as:<br><br>No carpets. No curtains. No books – <i>
  <b>What???</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513932075ra/24735665.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>No pets. No kids. No mess – I beg your pardon? Who are you to tell me if I have to clean my apartment or not. No, sir no. What if, I want to keep it like that?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514739767ra/24807409.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Punish me then. I bet Jane, the girl who lived there before, would love to be punished.<br><br>Those rules were not just warning bells, they were warning bombs that had to make those women to run away. But of course they didn’t. No. They preferred to stay in a high-tech apartment and to fall for, – a perfectionist, a control freak and a creepy owner of this minimalistic apartment -, who have buried his late wife and son in this same apartment. Who knows maybe this minimalistic freak was the same person who killed his family. It was like I was watching a bad version of the Saw movies when the owner of One Folgate Street appeared with all those weird rules and proclaimed that a kind of game has begun. And may the odds be ever in your favour.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514739767ra/24807410.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then again, leaving in a super-clever-high-technological-environment was quite original and I wanted to enjoy the story but I just couldn’t especially after some crucial moments and messages of the book.<br><br>One of the most distasteful moments, especially after the events one of the main characters had to go thorough, was:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Yes, daddy. Yes"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514739767ra/24807411.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>
  <b>Seriously?</b>
</i><br><br>This was neither an erotic story nor a thriller. It was an attempt to combine those two genres. Therefore, if you go into this don’t expect those two components.<br><br>Secondly, both women were presented as weak-willed, indecisive, and obsessive personalities. I can’t stand when books present women as highly dependable individualities, who need a man, in order to change their lives. No. Women are strong, self-sufficient, courageous, and independent. They are responsible for their own fate.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514739767ra/24807412.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The girl before, was exactly this type of book, where both women preferred to be involved in an unhealthy sexual relationship just to feel what? Alive? A bad girl? What I want to say is that they could do a load of things in order to get relieved from the unfortunate events of their past. To demonstrate, they could be involved in voluntary organization to help the women with the same problems. There was an attempt to present one of the main characters in those patterns but I didn’t find it adequate. Identically, they could travel, meet people, learn to play piano, help the planet to become more sustainable. Anything. On the contrary, they assumed it would be more “reliable” to play with a rich, handsome, manipulative-daddy to get rid of their memories, pain and even all those traits that made them the people they were.<br><br>Besides, there were a lot of racism issues all over the story. I just don’t want to give away the plot so please forgive me if the following won’t make any sense. The bad boys of the story were black and working class. Come on. <br><br><i>
  <b>Seriously? </b>
</i> <br><br>Likewise, there was a controversial issue about people with a Down Syndrome and whereas they have to be born or not. This was one of the main reasons which made me highly disapprove this controlling freak, whose name I don’t even remember.<br><br>Consequently, this book wasn’t for me. I would prefer a different ending just to be able to say<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514739767ra/24807413.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17576168458665224347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaceey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaceey" href="/user/show/13442817-kaceey">Kaceey</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1757472547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer349862496861002834"><b>3.5</b><br/>The perfect home to lease. Custom-designed and built by a world renowned architect. Every modern amenity one could possibly dream up… some even beyond your imagination! What’s not to like?<br/>Just one small hitch. You must agree to the terms set forth by the architect. Rules covering seemingly everything from A – Z, regarding what may be brought into the apartment. Not the least of which includes no pets or even children.<br/><br/>Emma is looking for a safe haven. Her last flat was broken into and ransacke</span>
  <span id="freeText349862496861002834" style="display:none"><b>3.5</b><br />The perfect home to lease. Custom-designed and built by a world renowned architect. Every modern amenity one could possibly dream up… some even beyond your imagination! What’s not to like?<br />Just one small hitch. You must agree to the terms set forth by the architect. Rules covering seemingly everything from A – Z, regarding what may be brought into the apartment. Not the least of which includes no pets or even children.<br /><br />Emma is looking for a safe haven. Her last flat was broken into and ransacked while she was home. Still terrified, she feels no place is safe until she happens upon One Folgate Street.<br /><br />Jane is busy putting her life back together after losing her baby. She’s drawn to the beauty and originality of this incredible home. Of course she can handle a few bizarre rules! No problem.<br /><br />Told through both Emma and Jane’s POV in 2 separate timelines. <br /><br /><b>Personal anecdote:</b> My husband and I rented a cabin for a weekend vacation. As we checked-in, we were handed a ridiculously large book of rules and regulations. We were expected to read and abide by them! (Can’t make this stuff up!) Needless to say we checked out the next day. Early! That was several years ago...but we still chuckle about it! <br /><br />This book brought back those wacky memories for me. Although this contract went way above and beyond our rule book! I still think Emma and Jane should have hightailed it out of there as soon as they poured over the rules!<br /><br /><i>If it sounds too good to be true...well you know...</i><br /><br />A great premise for a book and engaging writing quickly drew me in. Though it did veer off and become a little too fifty shades(ish) at times. I’m a little torn and maybe disappointed in the ending. I think a few of the final chapters could have been skipped to stay on point just a bit better. Though overall, I did enjoy it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="349862496861002834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1729241491?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729241491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4304072402326685452">I am in the minority with my feelings about <i>The Girl Before</i>--this book has received excellent reviews, but it just didn’t work for me. <br/><br/>The premise is intriguing: What if you had the opportunity to live in the perfect house designed by a famous architect for a low price? The only catch is that the house will record data, and track your every move. Also, the lease will have over 200 clauses, including such things as not leaving anything on the floor and no books allowed! There will be the occasion</span>
  <span id="freeText4304072402326685452" style="display:none">I am in the minority with my feelings about <i>The Girl Before</i>--this book has received excellent reviews, but it just didn’t work for me. <br /><br />The premise is intriguing: What if you had the opportunity to live in the perfect house designed by a famous architect for a low price? The only catch is that the house will record data, and track your every move. Also, the lease will have over 200 clauses, including such things as not leaving anything on the floor and no books allowed! There will be the occasional quiz, and if you don’t comply or do well, appliances will stop working. Some would run for the hills, but to others, it sounds like a dream come true! The perfect house will help people reach levels of perfection they never thought they could achieve. This is the house located on One Folgate Street. <br /><br />The Girl Before tells the stories of Emma and Jane, two occupants who lived in One Folgate.. Emma died under mysterious circumstances while living in One Folgate Street, and Jane is the current occupant. Both women look alike, and both were involved with Edward Monkton, the architect and mastermind behind One Folgate Street--both also happen to bear an eerie resemblance to Edward’s deceased wife. Jane begins to investigate Emma’s death, and by doing so, puts herself in danger.<br /><br />While the premise was interesting, it felt like the author was trying to cram pieces into a puzzle that didn’t fit. As a result, everything unraveled and it all became a little ridiculous. <i>The Girl Before</i> was just not my cup of tea.<br /><br />I received a copy of this book from NetGalley and the publisher in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32054243-the-girl-before">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42481357-melisa?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42481357-melisa?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42481357-melisa?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1785352183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18105946209513874485"><b>Update</b>: I just read that Ron Howard is going to direct the movie adaptation of this book. I can't wait!<br/><br/>Wow! Book slump averted! A thriller has not made me this excited since Megan Miranda's <b>All the Missing Girls</b>. <br/><br/>The story is told in alternating chapters between Emma, the girl before, and Jane, the current tenant of a very unique flat. While both women are searching for a living situation within their budgets in expensive London, their brokers both mention a possible solution. One Folgate Street</span>
  <span id="freeText18105946209513874485" style="display:none"><b>Update</b>: I just read that Ron Howard is going to direct the movie adaptation of this book. I can't wait!<br /><br />Wow! Book slump averted! A thriller has not made me this excited since Megan Miranda's <b>All the Missing Girls</b>. <br /><br />The story is told in alternating chapters between Emma, the girl before, and Jane, the current tenant of a very unique flat. While both women are searching for a living situation within their budgets in expensive London, their brokers both mention a possible solution. One Folgate Street has been designed by an architectural genius, Edward Monkford, but in order to live there, one must pass a series of vetting including a multi paged questionnaire and interview. This is where things just begin to get weird. I fear saying much more will give away the twists and turns within these pages. <br /><br />(As an aside, Emma's chapters are told without any quotation marks in the dialogue. While it takes some time to getting used to, it is very effective in differentiating between the two women's chapters. However I am completely curious as to why the author chose to use this device, if anyone knows, fill me in.)<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed how the author portrayed One Folgate - the apartment itself takes on a life of its own and becomes a central character in the story. <br /><br />There are multiple triggers within this book. I feel if I mention them here, they would be spoilers. So. Pretty much, if it's a trigger you can think of, it's here. Reader be warned!<br /><br />I've heard this author is writing under a pseudonym, and I am completely curious as to who masterminded this intricate story. <br /><br />If you need to have likable characters to enjoy a book, pass on this one. If you are very sensitive in nature and have some triggers, pass. If you want a wild roller coaster ride of ups and downs and rights and lefts, pick this one up! You won't be able to put it down.<br /><br />Thank you to Netgalley and the publisher for a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4283292484220897295">*3.5 STARS*. <br/><br/>One Folgate Street is a state of the art award winning property. The rent is pretty reasonable too, but it's tenants must be prepared to give up all their possessions - no books, throws, cushions, photos, no personal effects, nothing except the bare minimum of clothes. Then there are the other rules - hundreds of them, seemingly waiting to trip you up, catch you unawares. There are also regular questions to answer, very personal and intrusive questions. The fact is, whoever becomes </span>
  <span id="freeText4283292484220897295" style="display:none">*3.5 STARS*. <br /><br />One Folgate Street is a state of the art award winning property. The rent is pretty reasonable too, but it's tenants must be prepared to give up all their possessions - no books, throws, cushions, photos, no personal effects, nothing except the bare minimum of clothes. Then there are the other rules - hundreds of them, seemingly waiting to trip you up, catch you unawares. There are also regular questions to answer, very personal and intrusive questions. The fact is, whoever becomes this property's tenant must be willing to be completely controlled.<br /><br />Emma needs to find a new place to live after a traumatic break-in. She can't find anything that is affordable, that is until she finds One Folgate Street. She loves it on sight but Edward the architect, insists on complete control in order to transform his tenants to suit the space in which they're living, and he certainly manages to do that.<br /><br />Jane also needs a new start after a personal tragedy - she too loves the property but is also drawn to Edward, its creator. She soon discovers that Emma met an untimely death in the house, and begins investigating just what really happened there.<br /><br />The narrative certainly kept my attention, I really wanted to know what happened to Emma, but I found it hard to believe in Edward, AND his rules, so really that stopped me from rating this one any higher.<br /><br />*Thank you to Netgalley &amp; Quercus for my ARC in exchange for a fair and honest review*</span>

<div id="review_2148225961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2148225961" />
    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2148225961?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32054243-the-girl-before">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=books-bejeweled">books-bejeweled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2148225961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer995648999037765642"><b>3 stars</b><br/><br/>For a book that is centered on a minimalist approach to life in a spare, modern home--this story is a bit messy! Oh, the irony. Marie Kondo, where are you? Clean up on aisle 5!!<br/><br/>I was immediately sucked in to the plot. Most readers will identify with the depressing search for an affordable place to live that is also stylish and meets all of our must-haves. It doesn’t exist. <br/><br/>What if you find out that there is a gorgeous modern home available for very little moolah? It has everything. State </span>
  <span id="freeText995648999037765642" style="display:none"><b>3 stars</b><br /><br />For a book that is centered on a minimalist approach to life in a spare, modern home--this story is a bit messy! Oh, the irony. Marie Kondo, where are you? Clean up on aisle 5!!<br /><br />I was immediately sucked in to the plot. Most readers will identify with the depressing search for an affordable place to live that is also stylish and meets all of our must-haves. It doesn’t exist. <br /><br />What if you find out that there is a gorgeous modern home available for very little moolah? It has everything. State of the art technology is hidden within the pale gray stone walls. Everything you could ever want in high end luxury is available at your fingertips in this smart house. <br /><br />The famous architect, Edward Monkford, is the owner and creator of this modernistic miracle. But, there is a catch to scoring the rental deal of the century. Of course. <br /><br />You must take a lengthy personality assessment quiz. You must be personally approved by Monkford himself. You <b>MUST SIGN A CONTRACT</b> that states you will never leave a dirty glass out on the kitchen counter, or leave anything out anywhere in the house at anytime. You may not move in anything but your essentials. <b>NOT EVEN BOOKS!</b> Yes, you heard me right, books are not essential according to Monkford. (insert crying laughing face) And, while you’re signing this contract so fast, hoping Monkford won’t change his mind about you, watch out! You may be literally signing your life away.<br /><br />Emma and Jane are our alternating narrators, Emma is THEN and Jane is NOW, so that makes Emma THE GIRL BEFORE. Except, not really. There was a girl before Emma, Monkford’s wife, Elizabeth. Uggggghhhhh. Got all that?<br /><br /><b>Co-winky-dink alert:</b> The three women look just alike. They all fall in love with the starchitect (at different points in time). They are all struggling with personal crises in their lives. Three people have actually died there. Will Jane be next?<br /><br />Monkford is a controlling narcissist. The damaged women all fall under his commanding spell. Gag. <i>GETTING VERY TIRED OF THESE WIMPY FEMALE CHARACTERS!</i> C’mon fiction writers! <br /><br />The story just wasn’t compelling enough to keep me hooked after the first few chapters. It lingers on with the biggest challenge keeping Emma and Jane separate in your mind. Although the audio book is very well done by the narrator, the chapters are way too confusing to listen and follow. I ended up reading the book on Kindle. <br /><br />A minor stylistic point, but what the heck with the way this author writes dialogue? The pseudo named JP Delaney uses the word "go" instead of "said". No quotation marks either. I’m okay with that, although it puts the action in a passive present tense. Weird. I truly hate reading sentences like this:<br /><br /><b>I don’t know, I go. Welcome Emma and Simon, she goes.</b><br /><br />English teachers will want to stab themselves in the eye when they read this. Please, please don't let this be a new writing trend!<br /><br />The novel is slick and mildly interesting. There is a twist at the end, thank goodness, but it misses the mark and tries too hard to be cool. Hoping Ron Howard will ratchet up the coolness factor in his new movie version. </span>
  <a data-text-id="995648999037765642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789516550?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norma" href="/user/show/41400192-norma">Norma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789516550" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1116627034642641733">If I am rating this solely on my review rating system this book gets no more than 2 stars from me.  It was just okay and for the most part it wasn’t an enjoyable read for me.  I listened to the audio version of this book and what I did really like though was the narrators as it was performed very well by Emilia Fox, Finty Williams, and Lisa Aagaard Knudsen.<br/><br/>While the premise of THE GIRL BEFORE by J.P. DELANEY did sound quite intriguing to me and there was definitely something about this book that</span>
  <span id="freeText1116627034642641733" style="display:none">If I am rating this solely on my review rating system this book gets no more than 2 stars from me.  It was just okay and for the most part it wasn’t an enjoyable read for me.  I listened to the audio version of this book and what I did really like though was the narrators as it was performed very well by Emilia Fox, Finty Williams, and Lisa Aagaard Knudsen.<br /><br />While the premise of THE GIRL BEFORE by J.P. DELANEY did sound quite intriguing to me and there was definitely something about this book that did hold my interest enough to keep me wanting to listen to the end.  There were just way too many things included in this storyline that just didn’t work for me and just seemed ridiculous. It just wasn’t my cup of tea.  At one point I wasn’t even going to finish listening to it as I was so turned off and it had a 50 shades kind of feel to it which is just not my kinda thing. However I continued as I did need to know how this was going to play out.  I am glad I am finished.<br /><br />What I did like was the format of the storyline as it was delivered in alternating short chapters between then and now mirroring the points of view of our two main characters; Emma the previous tenant and Jane the current tenant. Which I found to be an enjoyable way to listen to this story.<br /><br />All of Brenda’s and my reviews can be found on our sister blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">http://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756952341?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/9472704-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756952341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11821453555664389760">I received a copy of The Girl Before through NetGalley for an honest review. My thanks to Ballantine Books and to J.P. Delaney for the opportunity.<br/><br/>To control or to be controlled?......now that is the question.<br/><br/>The Girl Before has more wicked cogs in the wheel than a jacked-up Monster truck in high gear. And that wheel keeps turning and turning throughout the entire story. Some days that wheel grinds in the down and dirty. Some days it revs up speed and gains relentless traction.<br/><br/>Emma Matthews live</span>
  <span id="freeText11821453555664389760" style="display:none">I received a copy of The Girl Before through NetGalley for an honest review. My thanks to Ballantine Books and to J.P. Delaney for the opportunity.<br /><br />To control or to be controlled?......now that is the question.<br /><br />The Girl Before has more wicked cogs in the wheel than a jacked-up Monster truck in high gear. And that wheel keeps turning and turning throughout the entire story. Some days that wheel grinds in the down and dirty. Some days it revs up speed and gains relentless traction.<br /><br />Emma Matthews lives in the "once upon a gruesome time". Her spin in the wheel is entitled "Then". Emma and her boyfriend, Simon, are desperate for a safe haven after Emma is attacked in their present apartment. Fear makes you snap at quick decisions. Desperately, they apply for residency at a slick, state-of-the-art building. Even all the mind-blowing questionaires and restrictions don't deter them. No books (Ah, c'mon now!), no cushions, no placemats, no personal items left out. And they sign on the dotted line.<br /><br />Edward is the award winning architect and owner of this granite luxury edifice. He lost his wife and young son in a freak accident not long before. Living in Japan for a time afterwards, Edward returns to manage his property. And manage he does......quite to the nth degree.<br /><br />Jane Cavendish resides in the time slot entitled "Now". She will be the latest occupant of One Folgate Street. She recently gave birth to a stillborn little girl and has been devastated by the loss. Jane, too, is seeking solace behind the walls of this highly efficient building. Although this "covenant" seems highly imposing and limiting, Jane signs on the dotted line as well.<br /><br />Soon Jane begins to connect occurrences in her present situation to those of Emma in the past. Things just don't seem to add up. What actually happened to Emma?<br /><br />The Girl Before will be made into a movie by Ron Howard. It brings to mind a Julia Roberts movie (1991) called Sleeping With the Enemy. Remember how the canned goods and spices had to be stacked just so and the towels primly arranged on the rack? Oh, sweetheart, this is just the beginning......<br /><br />The Girl Before is one sharp-ended story that reaches deeply into the slightly tilted minds of its characters. Not everyone has a solid handle on their secrets in this one. Appearances can be deceiving. "No one who lives in this house should expect privacy." And privacy was left on the curb just footsteps from the entrance of that solid front door.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11821453555664389760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1891266471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1891266471" />
    <a title="Christine PNW" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5664767-christine-pnw"><img alt="Christine PNW" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449339788p2/5664767.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1891266471?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine PNW" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine PNW" href="/user/show/5664767-christine-pnw">Christine PNW</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891266471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3532000839826764121">Overhyped and underwhelmed.<br/><br/>Honestly, I should've known better. I mean, first of all, it had the word "Girl" in the title, which was a clue that it would be bandwaggoning the tail end of a trend. And then, once I finished reading it, I found Emily May's review that made the connection between this book and Fifty Shades of Grey.<br/><br/>Here is a list of all of the things I hated about this book:<br/><br/>1. Edward. His character was completely unconvincing. I haven't read FSoG and I have no plans to do so. However,</span>
  <span id="freeText3532000839826764121" style="display:none">Overhyped and underwhelmed.<br /><br />Honestly, I should've known better. I mean, first of all, it had the word "Girl" in the title, which was a clue that it would be bandwaggoning the tail end of a trend. And then, once I finished reading it, I found Emily May's review that made the connection between this book and Fifty Shades of Grey.<br /><br />Here is a list of all of the things I hated about this book:<br /><br />1. Edward. His character was completely unconvincing. I haven't read FSoG and I have no plans to do so. However, that book has permeated the pop culture to the level that even I was able to draw the parallels between his character and Christian Grey. "I don't do traditional relationships," he purred, smoothly. "I'm coming over, and I'm going to take you to bed," he told her (completely out of the blue, by the way). If a man said that to me, I'd meet him at the door with a sledgehammer and a restraining order. Not that Jane would have a sledgehammer, since it's probably a violation of the preposterous rules that she agreed to before moving into the house to have a sledgehammer. <br />2. BDSM. Never have I been so unconvinced of spanking in a book. Never.<br />3. BDSM (again). When Emma called him "daddy" it literally came out of nowhere. The ultimate sexual non sequitur. Where in the hell did that come from? <br />4. Emma. Shut your fucking face you lying liar who lies. Honestly, she was one of the most unlikeable female characters in any book ever. She lied about everything. Everything that made her sympathetic turned out to be entirely false. There were three sociopaths in this book, and she was one of them. Are we supposed to like her? I'm unclear on this point.<br />5. Jane. She is basically the equivalent of that dumb blonde in a horror movie who hides behind the wall of whirling knives instead of running the fuck away while she can. <br />6. It's treatment of trauma was totally surface and entirely based on the author's idea of what some one who has experienced trauma might do. <br />7. The house itself was entirely creepy and no one would ever live there. People who are alive, and who are not wax statues, do things that create clutter and mess. Even the tidiest house will have, at a minimum, a family photo displayed. Living in that house would be like living in a mausoleum. No one would voluntarily live in a mausoleum before they had actually become a corpse.<br />8. The twist. I figured it out. Go away.<br />9. The dual narrations in opposing chapters. Tired. Trite. Been done.<br />10. The ending. Nice gimmick.<br /><br />So, yeah, there really wasn't anything I liked about this book. I should've known better, really, than to buy it. But can this trend of unrealistic characters and their behaviors in "realistic" fiction be over now, please?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3532000839826764121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1880557798" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1880557798" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1880557798?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1880557798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10392024566978293805">This book is very manipulative and, clearly, deceptive.<br/><br/>If that bothers you – and if you generally dislike far-fetched cases – I suggest you read something less convoluted. <br/><br/>By ‘‘manipulative,’’ I mean you’re more than pushed into liking specific characters and disliking others. So you do that. But despite having your thoughts about characters shaped by the author, you’re still manipulated some more as the story progresses. <br/><br/>I don’t exactly like when that happens. I prefer to be exposed to all face</span>
  <span id="freeText10392024566978293805" style="display:none">This book is very manipulative and, clearly, deceptive.<br /><br />If that bothers you – and if you generally dislike far-fetched cases – I suggest you read something less convoluted. <br /><br />By ‘‘manipulative,’’ I mean you’re more than pushed into liking specific characters and disliking others. So you do that. But despite having your thoughts about characters shaped by the author, you’re still manipulated some more as the story progresses. <br /><br />I don’t exactly like when that happens. I prefer to be exposed to all facets of someone’s personality and then be able to decide for myself who deserves justice and who doesn’t. <br /><br />This mystery novel is engrossing, despite it not giving us the liberty of making our own opinions on the protagonists and antagonists until the very end. The short chapters surely had their role to play in my being unable to put this book down.<br /><br />It’s slow, partly because it’s a mystery novel. If you’re familiar with the genre, you know that these types of novels take time to pick up because it’s all about the building part. It takes time for Jane to discover someone died in the house and it takes time for Emma to feel scared. That’s when things really become interesting.<br /><br />The death thing confused me, since I thought real estate agents were supposed to disclose info like that – especially when the previous tenants have died. But I guess there are places where no such law exists. Bummer, but it worked in the author’s favour. <br /><br />I enjoyed seeing this book shift from mystery to psychological thriller. I’m definitely the type to enjoy action in my plots, so I couldn’t do anything else but welcome the darker side of THE GIRL BEFORE, even if it takes time to reach that point. <br /><br />The characters also take time to become important in the reader’s eyes; most likely because they seem so normal, but that’s probably done on purpose to give the effect that this kind of story could happen to you or me. Anyone at all. <br /><br />But don’t worry; it’s very, very unlikely. Sleep tight now. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10392024566978293805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
